  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6aac035f-828f-412d-b0e5-50b331bbe980'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText455177044795200187" style="display:none">A princess on her own . . .<br /><br />Mia has been invited to speak at a gala for Domina Rei, an elite society of powerful businesswomen. But what could she possibly have to say? Now that Michael has broken things off, Mia can barely get out of bed, and her parents are making her see a "therapist." School, where Lilly still refuses to speak to her and Lana suddenly wants to be bff, is a total nightmare. Even J.P.'s efforts to cheer Mia up (he's being really sweet!) aren't helping. What's a royal to do?<br /><br />Just when things couldn't get worse, Mia uncovers an old family secret, a long-forgotten diary of a teenage princess of Genovia. It could be just the thing to help Mia write her speech--but it might also change the fate of the Renaldos forever.</span>

<div id="review_183252587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183252587" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947264-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389401312p2/3947264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183252587?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3947264-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=great-characters">great-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=little-romance">little-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=love-geometry">love-geometry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183252587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12290231241686033705">Hmmm.<br/><br/>This book was fighting a losing battle against itself.<br/><br/>What do I mean by that? I guess... just that parts of it were great; other parts made me want to barf. Which, for me, makes it a typical Meg Cabot experience. I feel like we're destined to not click, Meg and I.<br/><br/><b>The Great</b><br/>Maybe it's just that I've read so many of Mia's diaries, but these characters are starting to find a place in my heart. Especially Tina and Boris. Bless their hearts. (Lilly, too, is starting to feel like a real person... </span>
  <span id="freeText12290231241686033705" style="display:none">Hmmm.<br /><br />This book was fighting a losing battle against itself.<br /><br />What do I mean by that? I guess... just that parts of it were great; other parts made me want to barf. Which, for me, makes it a typical Meg Cabot experience. I feel like we're destined to not click, Meg and I.<br /><br /><b>The Great</b><br />Maybe it's just that I've read so many of Mia's diaries, but these characters are starting to find a place in my heart. Especially Tina and Boris. Bless their hearts. (Lilly, too, is starting to feel like a real person... but I don't want to bless her heart.)<br /><br />I really liked the semi-plot twist toward the end. For those of you who've read the series or just don't care about spoilers: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Genovia is now a constitutional monarchy. Alright! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I didn't see that coming at all. Not that seeing it coming would even be <i>possible</i>. It wasn't that type of plot twist.<br /><br />Lana's increased presence was very welcome to me. Some of my favorite parts of the book were due to her. What a champ. <br /><br /><b>The Barfable</b><br />It got more tolerable as the book progressed, but at its introduction Mia's mental health problems seemed more like a transparent PSA than an authentic plot development. <br /><br />Maybe I should be used to this by now, but it drives me straight up crazy when Mia is so clueless about everything. I just want to shake her. J.P. being in love with her was so darn obvious. And conflicting, as I will dwell on later.<br /><br />Ok so... this is maybe one of my biggest complaints that applies to the series as a whole. Why do I care so little about Michael? Is it my fault? Because Mia is unhealthily obsessed with him, and, from what I've seen, hard-core fans of the series are head over heels for the boy as well. But he's been included so infrequently in the series (apart from the first few books) that I just plain don't give a rip about their relationship.<br /><br /><b>The Weird</b><br />So, given what I just said about not caring about Michael, you'd think I'd be cheering on Mia+J.P. as a couple like nobody's business. I feel like I should be, too. I suspect that if I was a student at Albert Einstein, I would have the creepiest crush on J.P. that the world has ever seen. But, as a reader, I just feel conflicted. Who is this kid? He seems too good to be true. And his doggedness in leaving Mia's Friend Zone would normally seem sweet to me (and it kind of does, still), but I just can't bring myself to root for the poor boy. Find love, J.P. dear, but not with Mia. Okay.<br /><br /><br /><br />I'm not sure why I wrote such a long review for a book I don't care much about, but I guess it's my way of making up for the fact that most of my PD reviews have been munchkins. <br /><br />P.S. Lilly is stupid and I hope Mia tells her so in the next (and final) book. OMG I'M ALMOST DONE!!!!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12290231241686033705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37578397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37578397" />

<div id="review_608555612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608555612" />
    <a title="Abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7621490-abby"><img alt="Abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470975395p2/7621490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/608555612?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/7621490-abby">Abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer608555612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6334075546321668753"><b> This is the first book in this series that I felt I could make a full-sized review on and that's because I think this one was my favorite so far. </b> <br/><br/><b> Characters: </b><br/><b> Mia: </b> I finally fully loved Mia's character in a book. I think she changed and grew a lot from the last book and she's finally realizing things that need to be realized. I almost think she's more relatable now that she's gone through her transformation. Her breakdown was believable and consistent with her character through the series. <br/><b> </b></span>
  <span id="freeText6334075546321668753" style="display:none"><b> This is the first book in this series that I felt I could make a full-sized review on and that's because I think this one was my favorite so far. </b> <br /><br /><b> Characters: </b><br /><b> Mia: </b> I finally fully loved Mia's character in a book. I think she changed and grew a lot from the last book and she's finally realizing things that need to be realized. I almost think she's more relatable now that she's gone through her transformation. Her breakdown was believable and consistent with her character through the series. <br /><b> Michael: </b> As I've said in my review of the other books, I love Michael. I think he's great for Mia. That being said, I think I liked this book more because Michael WASN'T in it that much. This is because I do think that Mia needed some time apart from him to mature a bit and find out who she is when they're separate. <br /><b> Lilly: </b> And I think things finally went down with Lilly that I think have needed to go down for a while. Lilly has been frustrating me since the beginning (as she's meant to). Mia's always been loyal to her (I'd say that loyalty is one of Mia's best traits) and yet I'm not sure Lilly has never really deserved it. But, in truth, she's a very consistent and well-written character. You know why she's doing the things she's doing (even if Mia doesn't).<br /><br /><b> More Characters: </b><br /><b> Boris: </b> Such a sweetie. I love him and Tina together and I absolutely love how he's such a good friend to Mia (and everyone for that matter). He's the character in this series that I think I've slowly grown to love the most.<br /><b> JP: </b> I like him a surprising amount...Like, way more than I thought I would. I thought I would hate him just because he's, you know, not Michael. But, Meg Cabot did a great job of making him not some placeholder character. He was a great character in his own right. I can't say I'm rooting for him, but I will say I love him.<br /><b> Tina: </b> SO SWEET. Another one of my favorites (and she has been since the very first book). She's such a perfect friend to Mia (who has always needed a friend the exact opposite of what Lilly is).<br /><br /><b> This is one of the series that I honestly never thought I'd ever read. It was one of the ones that I thought I had stumbled onto too late to truly enjoy. But I'm finding myself really sad that the next book I have to read is the last one. Sure, these books are ridiculous and silly and not high-literature or whatever, but these characters became real to me in a way that few do. They felt like real people and real friends that I could laugh with and cry with. I'm glad that I gave them a chance and took the time to read this ridiculous and silly and just plain fun series. </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6334075546321668753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3007514483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3007514483" />
    <a title="Reading Relish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61495116-reading-relish"><img alt="Reading Relish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597187862p2/61495116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3007514483?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Relish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Relish" href="/user/show/61495116-reading-relish">Reading Relish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330448550" href="/book/show/2641860-to-the-nines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=diaries">diaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=school">school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3007514483&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3007514483" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9825573259615865971">I still don’t trust him...<br/><br/>[REVIEW]<br/><br/>I wasn’t as frustrated with this book as I was with Princess on the Brink. I was just more…confused. The Princess Diaries is known for it’s chaotic plots and unexpected twists, but this was…something else. While I did understand everything by the end, I felt mostly lost reading this.<br/><br/>MY THOUGHTS ON...<br/><br/>WHAT I LIKED:<br/><br/>•I liked how supportive and patient Tina was of Mia. She’s the kind of friend you can rely on being there for you when you’re at your worst. Tina invite</span>
  <span id="freeText9825573259615865971" style="display:none">I still don’t trust him...<br /><br />[REVIEW]<br /><br />I wasn’t as frustrated with this book as I was with Princess on the Brink. I was just more…confused. The Princess Diaries is known for it’s chaotic plots and unexpected twists, but this was…something else. While I did understand everything by the end, I felt mostly lost reading this.<br /><br />MY THOUGHTS ON...<br /><br />WHAT I LIKED:<br /><br />•I liked how supportive and patient Tina was of Mia. She’s the kind of friend you can rely on being there for you when you’re at your worst. Tina invited Mia to binge watch movies, encouraged her to keep going to school, and never told Mia to “get over” her breakup with Michael. Getting to see their friendship was very sweet! Looking back, I’ve realize Tina was always a better friend than Lilly (I’d say “Sorry, Lilly”, but honestly, I’m so done with her. Lilly accused Mia of being self-absorbed in this book, but let’s be real—Lilly hardly ever listened to Mia’s concerns throughout the series).<br /><br />•One thing that never gets old for me are all the references to the Disney adaptation of The Princess Diaries. I always laugh when Mia roasts the movies, talking about inaccurate they are to her real life. She doesn’t even reference Anne Hathaway, Julie Andrews, or even Disney. You just know they’re the movies based on how she describes them!<br /><br />•I did like the discussion of sexism and double standards, specifically during that reveal about her ancestor Amelia. It didn’t surprise me that Grandmere was against making Genovia a democracy. What did bother me was how Mia’s dad reacted. I’m glad Mia called him out on it, though, saying he would take Amelia seriously if she was a man. Hopefully he’ll come to his senses in the next book!<br /><br />CRITIQUES:<br /><br />•I wasn’t sure where the plot was going for a while. First there was the plot of Mia getting therapy. Then there was the whole subplot of Mia becoming friends with the high school mean girl Lana. THEN there was this whole investigation Mia did on one of her ancestors. THEN there was the anonymous website that was spewing hateful things about her called ihatemiathermopolis.com. THEN there was the whole thing with Mia and J.P. starting to have romantic feelings for each other. THEN...you get the picture z I felt like there was too much happening, and that this should’ve been narrowed down to only couple of subplots.<br /><br />•There were moments Mia’s therapist was spot on, and other times I got frustrated about some things he said that a therapist should NEVER say. One example is when the therapist called Mia “darling” when they first met, instead of just calling her Mia. Even though that was only one time, that didn’t sit right with me. I can’t believe no one questioned that.<br /><br />•The whole subplot with Lana. I get Mia was overwhelmed with the breakup, school, and her royal life. But the fact that she befriended LANA WEINBERGER out of blue??? There’s no way Lana would suddenly want to be friends with Mia without wanting some kind of personal gain. Yes, people change, but I’m not buying Lana’s sudden sympathy and friendliness (this was one thing I agree with Lilly about in the book). If it’s revealed that Lana is using Mia in the next book, I won’t be surprised. If not, then I’m going to be confused and honestly frustrated why Cabot suddenly decided to change Lana’s character.<br /><br />•Speaking of questioning people...This isn’t a critique of the book, but I do want to bring it up. I *still* don’t trust J.P. He was very sweet with Mia throughout this book, and I liked how he comforted her when she started crying over Michael. AND YET...he’s giving me subtle Hans-of-the-Southern-Isles vibes (Hans from Frozen). J.P. is just TOO perfect. He’s sweet, he’s charming, and he makes Mia laugh, which are all great traits! But ever since that hug and kiss (IN FRONT OF MICHAEL) the eighth book, I think it’s all an act. What he could possibly want from Mia, I’m not sure.<br /><br />FINAL THOUGHTS:<br /><br />I did like this a little bit more than the previous book. However, I still got confused and frustrated with many of the characters. But I am interested enough in seeing what’ll happen to Mia and everyone else in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9825573259615865971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3315077887&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3315077887" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer550572265943090666">In my opinion, this book was very surprising. I mean, there where things that I knew were true and some things that I knew that were going to happen, but the course of it was completely unexpected. Who would have said that Lily would create a website called, literally, ihatemiathermopolis? I know that she kind of lost her boyfriend to Mia, but it was just very very not nice. At first, she was Mia’s number one best friend, and then, turns into her worst enemy. And her friendship with Lana was pro</span>
  <span id="freeText550572265943090666" style="display:none">In my opinion, this book was very surprising. I mean, there where things that I knew were true and some things that I knew that were going to happen, but the course of it was completely unexpected. Who would have said that Lily would create a website called, literally, ihatemiathermopolis? I know that she kind of lost her boyfriend to Mia, but it was just very very not nice. At first, she was Mia’s number one best friend, and then, turns into her worst enemy. And her friendship with Lana was probably the most unexpected thing. But I really liked it. I really enjoyed Mia “fighting her demons” and getting better from depression. Now she has J.P, Tina, Boris, LANA...even Miachel is her friend now. And I am sure that her dad and grandmére will come along. I don’t know if I would have done the same(about the will), but I guess it was the right thing for Mia to do. She has grown a lot since the start, and I can’t wait to read the last book and see how everything is going to sort out. </span>

<div id="review_3174173761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3174173761" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8263750-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587266605p2/8263750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3174173761?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/8263750-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3174173761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4493394002685866277">2.5 stars. I said I was going to stop at the last book, but here I am. Torturing myself because I felt too close to the end of the series not to finish it. <br/><br/>Mia and Michael are officially done. Broken up with the love of her life, Mia doesn't know what to do with herself. She can't find the energy to get out of bed nor face the people at school where she knows they'll ask her about Michael. Not only that, but she doesn't have her best friend, Lily, to lean on anymore. <br/><br/>I know Mia was sorting throu</span>
  <span id="freeText4493394002685866277" style="display:none">2.5 stars. I said I was going to stop at the last book, but here I am. Torturing myself because I felt too close to the end of the series not to finish it. <br /><br />Mia and Michael are officially done. Broken up with the love of her life, Mia doesn't know what to do with herself. She can't find the energy to get out of bed nor face the people at school where she knows they'll ask her about Michael. Not only that, but she doesn't have her best friend, Lily, to lean on anymore. <br /><br />I know Mia was sorting through her breakup with Michael throughout this book, but man. MAN. She truly seems to lack a basic understanding of people and how things work. JP is consistently hanging around her and wanting to be close with her, but she always remains insistent that he doesn't like her. Now, I know that when you're in the thick of something like that it can be easy to miss, but despite her Tina and others constantly telling her that JP liked her, Mia never seemed to sit down and think about whether that was true or not. Please, just sit and think for a moment child. <br /><br />There were other moments and things she did that she never seemed to get exactly why people were upset with her. Mia had thought enough time had passed that she could just move on as if nothing happened. For some people, that may work, but she should have known that wasn't going to work in this instance. Apologize for goodness sake. <br /><br />I did like one moment towards the end though that did end up giving me a bit of hope for Mia and what she could become in the next two books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4493394002685866277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1184814720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184814720" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1184814720?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184814720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16281708352071448485">Eh 3.5 on reread. I did like this book, but upon reread I really got annoyed with some bits. The book feels a little PSA-y and honestly Mia wouldn't have what's considered clinical depression its situational depression at best. I wonder how Dr. Knutz would deal with someone with an actual mood disorder...actually I shudder at it. Also, upon reread the whole non-TV bit drove me mad. I am a grown ass woman now and I can still see myself throwing a huge fit over this logic. Also, it made me miss my</span>
  <span id="freeText16281708352071448485" style="display:none">Eh 3.5 on reread. I did like this book, but upon reread I really got annoyed with some bits. The book feels a little PSA-y and honestly Mia wouldn't have what's considered clinical depression its situational depression at best. I wonder how Dr. Knutz would deal with someone with an actual mood disorder...actually I shudder at it. Also, upon reread the whole non-TV bit drove me mad. I am a grown ass woman now and I can still see myself throwing a huge fit over this logic. Also, it made me miss my Lifetime movie list I relied on so much in this series.<br /><br />Also JP what a fake. It's painfully obvious with each reread what a little fool that boy was. <br /><br />To see full binge review click <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/04/08/the-unofficial-princess-diaries-binge-read-the-final-stretch/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />This was a really well book except…<br /><br />Mia’s not clinically depressed.<br /><br />I’m sorry.<br /><br />She was only in her pajamas for a week.<br /><br />Try living with someone who is clinically depressed and then try saying Mia is depressed.<br /><br />Um, no.<br /><br />That’s from my own personal experience though. Maybe if I hadn’t grown up with someone who suffered from depression, I wouldn’t have mind Dr. Knutz evaluation so much.<br /><br />And Mia’s parents, you really didn’t need to send her to a shrink. My parents would’ve just dragged me out of bed and threw me in the shower with my Hello Kitty pajamas on.<br /><br />Oh, and took my door off when I was in the shower.<br /><br />Or they would’ve just made me go to school in my pajamas.<br /><br />And if I ate all the leftovers and the Chinese food my sister would’ve probably decked me.<br /><br />Mia has it easy.<br /><br />That being said, while I thought a depression diagnosis was a little out there, one thing that I wish was addressed with Mia’s anxiety issues. But Dr. Knutz’s just kind of ignores that.<br /><br />He really annoys me.<br /><br />Then again, most shrinks do, so he was probably in character on that. Or as much as you can make a cowboy shrink be in character.<br /><br />I think what I liked about this one that it was really thought provoking. You had the mental illness factor and then the whole democracy for Genovia.<br /><br />All I can say is thank God for them because can you really imagine Mia as a leader?<br /><br />Um, yeah…didn’t think so.<br /><br />As much as I appreciate the idea of a giant cat rescue palace, it’s not exactly going to help a country’s GDP grow. Or for that matter, not getting in a war with Monaco or whoever about olive oil prices.<br /><br />Genovia really dodged a bullet there.<br /><br />I found the whole cover up with the grandmother and father a little eyebrow raising and wish we would’ve had another book or two to go through this.<br /><br />But again, there was a lot of good stuff here.<br /><br />I didn’t even mind the Jia stuff here. Though, it does make me sort of sad that they seemed sort of cute and enjoyable in this one and then…well, read Forever Princess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16281708352071448485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Tove" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44763681-tove"><img alt="Tove" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564421038p2/44763681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041029534?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tove" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tove" href="/user/show/44763681-tove">Tove</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28679075-bad-heir-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44763681-tove?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44763681-tove?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44763681-tove?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041029534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11832470254272791331">“Do one thing every day that frightens you,” Princess Mia advised her audience. “And never think that you can’t make a difference. Even if you’re only sixteen, and everyone is telling you that you’re just a silly teenage girl—don’t let them push you away. Remember one other thing Eleanor Roosevelt said: ‘No one can make you feel inferior without your<br/>consent.’ You are capable of great things—never let anyone try to tell you that just because you’ve only been a princess for twelve days, you don’t </span>
  <span id="freeText11832470254272791331" style="display:none">“Do one thing every day that frightens you,” Princess Mia advised her audience. “And never think that you can’t make a difference. Even if you’re only sixteen, and everyone is telling you that you’re just a silly teenage girl—don’t let them push you away. Remember one other thing Eleanor Roosevelt said: ‘No one can make you feel inferior without your<br />consent.’ You are capable of great things—never let anyone try to tell you that just because you’ve only been a princess for twelve days, you don’t know what you’re doing.” <br /><br />Overall it was an okay book but nothing more than that. I'm pretty sick of Princess diaries and luckily I only have two books left to read.<br />I think the depiction of depression was absolutely horrible, depression is in fact mental illness and very dangerous. It isn't something you should take lightly and you definitely shouldn't throw that word around without knowing what it is. I'm sure the author is very aware about what it is and what it does to people, BUT she failed to put that into words. Depression isn't when you and your boyfriend decide to take a break and you feel down afterwards (because who wouldn't feel sad about that?) and I got so annoyed when it was so obvious that she used "depression" to get sympathy for the main character. You can get depressed because of a breakup, yes, it's definitely possible. But it's absolutely normal to feel down the days after it happened.<br />Mia continues to appear whiny and immature, Lily is a horrible person and J.P appears to be even more annoying with his uncomfortable stalker behaviour, and basically the only thing I liked with this book was the relationship with Mia's former enemy Lana Weinberg and the development in that aspect plus Mia stepping up a bit in the end. But she's still very annoying. And she's suppose to be older than me. Geez. Meg Cabot is smart for sure, because now Mia can have her happily ever after with Michael without these complications mentioned in the previous books. Plus it's so stereotypical and it bothered me a bit (because why tell young girls that you have to transform and become hot because otherwise nobody wants you), the flat chested ugly girl with the unbearable hair FINALLY has her glow up while she's eating meat and stopped being a vegetarian and now FINALLY "grew up" and is hot so all the boys steal glances of her while they're passing by.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11832470254272791331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12008443532881366451">There are some books I read where I wrestle with my conscience: to list it on GoodReads, or not? And so far I've always come down on the side of listing them all, even though they may not all be books I want to cop to reading. I'm listing this one and not putting it in my update feed. Maybe it'll sneak under my Smart Friends' radars, because I read this and I feel a deep shame for that fact.<br/><br/>Somehow I've managed to avoid the Clique/Gossip Girl/A-List types, but this series has sucked me in and wo</span>
  <span id="freeText12008443532881366451" style="display:none">There are some books I read where I wrestle with my conscience: to list it on GoodReads, or not? And so far I've always come down on the side of listing them all, even though they may not all be books I want to cop to reading. I'm listing this one and not putting it in my update feed. Maybe it'll sneak under my Smart Friends' radars, because I read this and I feel a deep shame for that fact.<br /><br />Somehow I've managed to avoid the Clique/Gossip Girl/A-List types, but this series has sucked me in and won't let go. Part of it is that I do have parents at the library who ask if a series is appropriate for their kids of varying ages, and this is one of the books they ask about--because their 9- or 10-year-old daughters watched the first movie and want to read the books, but when does it take that turn for the Older Teen? (Answer: a couple of books ago.) <br /><br />Mia is battling a major depression after breaking up with her boyfriend, and the resulting disinterest in everything makes her whine a lot less about every other aspect of her life. But even without her incessant whining, this <i>drags</i>. We only get through about two weeks of minutiae: who's dating whom, X mad at Y, and lengthy IM sessions with what might be the most annoying Protagonist's Sidekick on the face of the planet. <br /><br />If you've been reading this series all along and have been enjoying it, there's nothing I can say to dissuade you from picking this one up, too. But if you're trying to quit, go for it. At the end of the book, very little has changed in Mia's life. Any major changes hinted at will have to be explored in the next volume, because this one ends just short of where the plot could (but probably won't) get interesting. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12008443532881366451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214737100" />
    <a title="hpboy13" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6427364-hpboy13"><img alt="hpboy13" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395922187p2/6427364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214737100?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hpboy13" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hpboy13" href="/user/show/6427364-hpboy13">hpboy13</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6427364-hpboy13?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6427364-hpboy13?shelf=best-of-ya">best-of-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214737100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12570764655349271842">Picking up right where #8 left off, this book shows Mia growing up and realizing who her true friends are. I thoroughly enjoyed it.<br/><br/>ETA 7 years later: Princess Mia continues the rejuvenation of the series that began in PD #8, building on its strengths to tell a compelling story while maintaining the series’ signature humor. Cabot does a great job showing Mia’s descent into depression, as well as her recovery. She also FINALLY addresses the fact that Lilly is pretty much the worst friend of all ti</span>
  <span id="freeText12570764655349271842" style="display:none">Picking up right where #8 left off, this book shows Mia growing up and realizing who her true friends are. I thoroughly enjoyed it.<br /><br />ETA 7 years later: Princess Mia continues the rejuvenation of the series that began in PD #8, building on its strengths to tell a compelling story while maintaining the series’ signature humor. Cabot does a great job showing Mia’s descent into depression, as well as her recovery. She also FINALLY addresses the fact that Lilly is pretty much the worst friend of all time (though I wish she would have spent more time on the schism in the friend group, instead of just throwing people onto various sides and calling it a day).<br /><br />The book finally let Mia’s relationship with Lana evolve, which I thought was a very deft touch (and definitely added humor through all the interactions between Lana and Mia’s friends). And it really brought home something Cabot has been deftly developing for most of the series – that Mia is no longer the awkward social pariah she was at the beginning of the series. It’s been a joy binging this series and seeing Mia develop into an awesome young woman, while laughing along the whole way.<br /><br />One thing that really disgruntled me, and it’s in the very first diary entry – Michael is made out to be a complete savage when Mia is talking about seeing Beauty and the Beast on Broadway. There’s a fine line between “boys’ll be boys and he’s not into it” and him snickering, complaining during the show, constantly leaving to play on his phone, and just generally being a disgrace. I get Cabot wanting to show the contrast between Michael and Mia/JP, but making him out to be so utterly contemptible is not the effect I think she was going for. I took a star off purely for ruining a perfectly good love interest like that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12570764655349271842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4498998997176509376">It was better than expected and I had a pretty decent time reading it. I am beginning to hope that maybe, just maybe Mia will grow up after all. There were some major developments. Lana Weinberger finally came over her animosity towards Mia. That was a major step forward.   <span id="freeText4498998997176509376" style="display:none">It was better than expected and I had a pretty decent time reading it. I am beginning to hope that maybe, just maybe Mia will grow up after all. There were some major developments. Lana Weinberger finally came over her animosity towards Mia. That was a major step forward. And Mia finally grew in places she frequently whined about in like, the first 5 books (THANK GOD for that). Mia's depression over her breakup with Michael and her emotional state was something I was intrigued by. I didn't feel sorry for her <i>at all</i> because the entire thing was her fault in the first place. Also intriguing was her relationship with J.P and I am looking forward to how that is resolved. Then there was this matter of Mia telling the world about her ancestress Amelie's executive order about dissolving the monarchy and making Genovia a democracy even though she was specifically told not to. I am all for equality and listening to teenagers' views instead of ignoring them but today that has just become an excuse to let young people do whatever they want, even in matters they are completely inexperienced and unaware of the repercussions. That is exactly what Mia did and that was wrong.<br /><p><b>P.S:</b> Only 3 books until this ends. YIPPEEEEEEEEE!!!</p></span>

<div id="review_11677632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11677632" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11677632?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11677632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7826063033316060258">This was one of the better ones of this series, to which I am totally and completely addicted. I laugh until I cry every time, but this one was actually . . . well, kinda serious, and that's a good thing. Michael has broken up with Mia, Lilly's not talking to her, she's discovered a terrible secret about Genovian history, and Cabot handles it all expertly. I've seen this book criticized for making light of depression, since Mia's parents send her to therapy because she's upset about Michael. As </span>
  <span id="freeText7826063033316060258" style="display:none">This was one of the better ones of this series, to which I am totally and completely addicted. I laugh until I cry every time, but this one was actually . . . well, kinda serious, and that's a good thing. Michael has broken up with Mia, Lilly's not talking to her, she's discovered a terrible secret about Genovian history, and Cabot handles it all expertly. I've seen this book criticized for making light of depression, since Mia's parents send her to therapy because she's upset about Michael. As someone who has suffered from depression, I was not offended at all. With everything that Mia was going through, I was glad that Cabot recognized that this would affect her emotional and psychological state. Although this was handled with Cabot's usual humorous, light touch, I thought that it was totally believable and handled quite well. In fact, this is probably my favorite next to the first book, because everything finally comes to a head: Lilly's fair-weather-friendship, her relationship with Michael, her duty as a royal, even her issues with Lana Weinberger. Two thumbs way, way up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7826063033316060258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330434959" href="/book/show/1924015.To_the_Nines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/572197-rachel-brand?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/572197-rachel-brand?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/572197-rachel-brand?shelf=2009">2009</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44937350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10361429726775277968">When I started to read this book I was worried that it was going to be another story full of whining and moaning from Mia, much like books 4 - 7, but thankfully it wasn't. There were some things which I liked about this book: the absence of Michael, who I always thought was unsuited for Mia; the absence of Lilly, who Mia should learn to stand up to; the story about the diary of Mia's ancestor, which was quite interesting; the subplot about Kenny - hilarious!; Mia realising that pining over Micha</span>
  <span id="freeText10361429726775277968" style="display:none">When I started to read this book I was worried that it was going to be another story full of whining and moaning from Mia, much like books 4 - 7, but thankfully it wasn't. There were some things which I liked about this book: the absence of Michael, who I always thought was unsuited for Mia; the absence of Lilly, who Mia should learn to stand up to; the story about the diary of Mia's ancestor, which was quite interesting; the subplot about Kenny - hilarious!; Mia realising that pining over Michael was going to get her nowhere; and Mia becoming friends with Lana, and her realisation that Lana isn't horrible, just shallow. Overall, this has to be one of the most realistic Princess Diaries books ever! I'm actually looking forward to reading the last book. I have to admit that the character of JP seems to be quite 2D at some points. But this didn't spoil the book too much, and it was an enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10361429726775277968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_25720303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25720303" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/612821-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1207007338p2/612821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25720303?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/612821-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">um, no one.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/612821-emma?shelf=meg-cabot">meg-cabot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/612821-emma?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer25720303&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25720303" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2782178616368838958">SPOILER! SPOILER! SPOILER! SPOILER!<br/><br/>Okay, I like the series. I wasn't real pleased with the one before this, but I was okay with it. The series is good. But this book was terrible. Mia acted like she was no one without Michael. And she's the one who dumped him, and when given the chance to tell him she din't want to be just friends, she didn't, and then spends the rest of the book whining about it! And I didn't like Lilly not being her friend. And she's so embarrassed about going to a therapist. </span>
  <span id="freeText2782178616368838958" style="display:none">SPOILER! SPOILER! SPOILER! SPOILER!<br /><br />Okay, I like the series. I wasn't real pleased with the one before this, but I was okay with it. The series is good. But this book was terrible. Mia acted like she was no one without Michael. And she's the one who dumped him, and when given the chance to tell him she din't want to be just friends, she didn't, and then spends the rest of the book whining about it! And I didn't like Lilly not being her friend. And she's so embarrassed about going to a therapist. And her dad was mean, about the whole not telling Grandmere about it, because it's not like it's a huge secret, or it shouldn't be. Her and JP getting together was really good, but I dind't really want JP and her to be together as Mia's rebound. And her and Lana being friends! What was up with that? In all, this is my least favorite book by Meg Cabot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2782178616368838958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VAHaRzhncAdpcse+LMROaz8EGwqhXC9jJkzpPGBjtybR7nSkh0JZDUNiAZq5QrY55H10pXxYexy7n4UiQw+YCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot">About Meg Cabot</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1532640822p3/11654.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot">Meg Cabot

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13883433988639958064">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText13883433988639958064" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>
